## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics in materials science (thermoelasticity and temperature-dependent constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which strongly indicates a constitutive law for a solid material. Common relationships include linear/nonlinear elasticity, plastic hardening laws, and thermal effects such as temperature-dependent modulus and thermal strain offsets.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear Hooke law (isothermal small-strain elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (elastic regime, constant modulus)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varies approximately linearly with temperature)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (polynomial-in-T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (curved E(T) dependence over a wider T range)
- Thermoelastic law with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after subtracting thermal expansion strain)
- Exponential thermal softening of modulus: sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) * epsilon (stiffness changes approximately exponentially with temperature over limited ranges)
- Rational thermal softening of modulus: sigma = (c0 / (c1 + T)) * epsilon (stiffness decreases with T and asymptotes at high T)
- Hollomon power-law hardening (isothermal plasticity surrogate): sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (empirical strain hardening beyond yield, no explicit yield offset)
- Ludwik-type offset power law: sigma = c0 + c1 * (epsilon + c2)**c3 (captures initial offset plus nonlinear hardening)
- Ramberg–Osgood implicit trend (explicit surrogate form): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2 (combines linear elasticity and nonlinear hardening in one explicit map)
- Thermally softened power-law hardening: sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) * epsilon**c2 (yield/flow stress reduced or increased with temperature while retaining hardening shape)
- Voce-type saturation hardening surrogate: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(c2 * epsilon)) (strain hardening approaches a saturation stress level)
- Entropic/polymer-like elasticity (neo-Hookean Cauchy stress in 1D form, using lambda = 1 + epsilon): sigma = (c0 * T) * ((1 + epsilon) - c1 / (1 + epsilon)**2) (rubber-like elasticity where modulus scales with absolute temperature)
- Smooth phase-transition-like blending of moduli: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (0.5 + 0.5 * tanh(c2 * (T - c3)))) * epsilon (captures glass-transition or softening around a characteristic temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: linear sigma–epsilon suggests sigma ≈ E(T)*epsilon, with curvature in epsilon indicating onset of nonlinear elasticity/plasticity.
- Thermal expansion compensation: dependence on (epsilon - c*(T - Tref)) indicates that part of strain is thermal (stress-free) and only the remainder generates stress.
- Thermal softening/stiffening: decreasing stress at fixed epsilon with increasing T often fits exp(c*T), 1/(T+c), or low-order E(T) polynomials multiplying epsilon.
- Hardening behavior: sigma growing sublinearly/superlinearly with epsilon is commonly captured by epsilon**n or mixed linear+power terms (elastic + plastic contributions).
- Saturation in hardening: approach to a limiting stress with increasing epsilon is naturally represented by c0 + c1*(1 - exp(c2*epsilon)).
- Polymer/entropic elasticity cue: sigma approximately proportional to T at fixed deformation (sigma ∝ T * f(epsilon)) suggests rubber-like networks rather than metal plasticity.
- Transition temperatures: rapid change of slope versus T (at fixed epsilon) is often better modeled by smooth-switch functions (tanh-based blending) than by a single global polynomial.
- Parameter separability: many constitutive forms are multiplicatively separable (sigma = f(T)*g(epsilon)); if data collapse occurs under rescaling by f(T), prefer separable structures.

GT: c0*epsilon*(-c1*(T - c2) + c3) - c4*(T - c5) + epsilon**c6*c7*(T - c8)

Let \(T_0=316.1945018642116\). Expand the GT:

\[
\begin{aligned}
\text{GT} &= 31.119982052994235\,\epsilon\big(-0.05295088673159155\,(T-T_0)+1\big) \\
&\quad -0.22554447458683766\,(T-T_0) \\
&\quad + 3.629301836816963\,\epsilon^{0.5975773894779193}(T-T_0).
\end{aligned}
\]

This is of the form
\[
\text{GT} = A\,T\epsilon + B\,\epsilon + C\,T + D + E\,T\,\epsilon^{p} + F\,\epsilon^{p}
\]
with **fixed nonzero** coefficients, where \(p=0.5975773894\) and crucially there is a **pure \(T\) term** (independent of \(\epsilon\)) coming from \(-0.2255(T-T_0)\), and also a **\(T\epsilon^{p}\)** term.

So any matching candidate must be able to produce simultaneously:
- a term proportional to \(T\epsilon\),
- a term proportional to \(T\epsilon^{p}\) with \(p\approx 0.5976\),
- a term proportional to \(T\) alone (no \(\epsilon\)),
- plus constants / \(\epsilon\)-only terms.

Now check candidates.

### Candidates 1–10 (all are polynomials in \(T\) times \(\epsilon\) plus \(\epsilon\)-only powers, but **no pure \(T\) term**)
1. \(T c0\epsilon + (\epsilon\text{-only terms}) + c2\). No \(T\) alone ⇒ cannot match GT’s \(-0.2255\,T\).
2. Same issue: only \(T\epsilon\) terms, no \(T\) alone.
3. Has \(T\epsilon^{c1}\) but still no pure \(T\) term.
4. Same as (1) with extra \(\epsilon\) term; still no pure \(T\).
5. Same: no pure \(T\).
6. Same: no pure \(T\).
7. Has \(T\epsilon^{c1}\) and an \(\exp(Tc9)\) factor; still no pure \(T\) term, and exponential-in-\(T\) would need to be killed (set coefficient 0), leaving no way to create pure \(T\).
8. Same: no pure \(T\).
9. Contains \(T*c1\) (pure \(T\)!) but also \(T*c1*\epsilon\) tied to same \(c1\). You could set \(c1\) to match the pure \(T\) coefficient, but then you are forced to also include an extra \(T\epsilon\) term with the same coefficient, which GT does **not** have (GT’s \(T\epsilon\) coefficient is different and already determined by the first big term). You could try to absorb by adjusting \(c0\), but then you’d still have the wrong decomposition because GT has exactly one \(T\epsilon\) coefficient; here it becomes \(c0+c1\) while pure \(T\) is \(c1\). That part is fine (choose \(c0\) accordingly), but the bigger blocker: there is still **no \(T\epsilon^{p}\)** term unless you use \(c7\epsilon^{c8}\) (but that is \(\epsilon\)-only, not multiplied by \(T\)). So cannot match.
10. Has pure \(T*c1\) and \(T*c0\epsilon\), but again no \(T\epsilon^{p}\) term.

### Candidates 11, 15 (rational \((\epsilon+1)^{-2}\) terms; still wrong structure)
11. Has \(T*c0\epsilon\), \(T*c2\epsilon\), \(T*c2\) (pure \(T\)), plus \(\epsilon\)-only powers. Still **no \(T\epsilon^{p}\)** term. The \((\epsilon+1)^{-2}\) term is \(T\)-scaled but not a power \(\epsilon^{0.5976}\); cannot equal \(T\epsilon^{p}\) on any plausible continuous domain (it’s a different functional form).
15. Similar: has \(T*c1\epsilon\) and \(T*c1\) and \(T*c0/(\epsilon+1)^2\). Again no \(T\epsilon^{p}\).

### Candidates 12–14, 16–20 (some have \(T\epsilon^{c1}\) but still miss required combination)
12. Has \(T*c0\epsilon^{c1}\) and also \(c7*\epsilon*(T+c8)^{c9}\). To get a linear \((T-T_0)\epsilon^{p}\) term you’d need \((T+c8)^{c9}\) to be linear in \(T\) (set \(c9=1\)), giving \(c7\epsilon(T+c8)\), which is \(T\epsilon\) plus \(\epsilon\) constant—not \(T\epsilon^{p}\). You could set \(c1=p\) to get \(T\epsilon^{p}\) from the first term, but then you still need a separate \(T\epsilon\) term and a pure \(T\) term; there is no pure \(T\) term here. So cannot match.
13. Has \(T*c0\epsilon^{c1}\) and \(T*c2\epsilon\) (good: can make \(T\epsilon^{p}\) and \(T\epsilon\)), but **no pure \(T\)** term.
14. Has \(T*c0\epsilon\) and \(T*c0\) (pure \(T\)) but they share the same \(c0\), forcing the pure \(T\) coefficient to equal the \(T\epsilon\) coefficient, which is not true in GT. Also no \(T\epsilon^{p}\).
16–17. Have pure \(T*c0\) but no \(T\epsilon^{p}\).
18. Has \(T*c0\epsilon^{c1}\), \(T*c2\epsilon\), and \(T*c2\) (pure \(T\)), but pure \(T\) and \(T\epsilon\) are tied to the same \(c2\) (since both use \(c2\)). GT needs independent coefficients for \(T\) and \(T\epsilon\). Even if you try to compensate by adjusting other terms, there is no other pure \(T\) source, so you cannot decouple them. Thus cannot match.
19. Similar tying issues plus extra \((\epsilon+1)^{-2}\) term; not match.
20. Has \(T*c0\epsilon^{c1}\) and \(T*c2\) (pure \(T\)), but **no \(T\epsilon\)** term unless you force \(c1=1\), which would destroy the needed \(p\approx0.5976\). So cannot match.

### Candidates 21–36 (no \(T\) dependence except via exp/log in some; GT is affine in \(T\))
21. Only \(T\) appears inside \(\exp(T*c9)\) multiplying an \(\epsilon\)-power term; GT is linear in \(T\), not exponential. You could set that coefficient to 0 to remove \(T\), but then you have no \(T\) dependence at all ⇒ cannot match.
22–29. No \(T\) at all ⇒ cannot match.
30. Has \(\exp(T*c7)\) multiplying an \(\epsilon\)-power; again not linear in \(T\) unless killed, which removes all \(T\) dependence.
31–36. No \(T\) dependence ⇒ cannot match.

### Candidates 37–49 (have \(T\epsilon^{c1}\) etc., but still cannot reproduce GT’s exact linear-in-\(T\) decomposition with a pure \(T\) term and both \(T\epsilon\) and \(T\epsilon^{p}\))
37. Adds \(\cos(T*c9)\) factor; GT has no oscillatory dependence. Setting that term’s coefficient 0 removes it; then candidate has no pure \(T\) term.
38. Has \(c7*\epsilon*\exp(T*c8)\) (nonlinear in \(T\)); must be killed; then no pure \(T\).
39. Has \(T*c0\epsilon^{c1}\) but no pure \(T\) term.
40. Has \(T*c0\epsilon^{c1}\) but no pure \(T\) term.
41. Has \(T^{c0}\) power; GT is linear in \(T\). You could set \(c0=1\) to get linear \(T\), but then term is \(T*c1*\epsilon^{c2}\) (no pure \(T\)), and still missing separate pure \(T\).
42. Has \(T*c0\epsilon^{c1}\) but no pure \(T\).
43. Same plus extra \((c8| \epsilon|+1)^{c9}\) (no \(T\)); still no pure \(T\).
44. Has \(T*c0\epsilon^{c1}\) but no pure \(T\).
45. Has \(T*c0\epsilon^{c1}\) but no pure \(T\).
46–48. Add log terms involving \(T\) or \(T\epsilon\) inside exponentials/logs; GT is affine in \(T\). Only way is to zero those terms, leaving no pure \(T\).
49. Has \(c7*\epsilon/(T+c8)\) (non-affine in \(T\)); must be killed; then no pure \(T\).

### Candidates 50–51 (contain \(T^2\); GT has no \(T^2\))
50. Has \(T^2*c0*\epsilon\). To remove \(T^2\) set \(c0=0\), but then you lose a needed \(T\epsilon\) contribution (and still no \(T\epsilon^{p}\) term). Not match.
51. Same issue.

**Key impossibility across the list:** GT requires *both* a pure \(T\) term and a \(T\epsilon^{0.5976}\) term and a \(T\epsilon\) term with independent coefficients. None of the candidates can generate all three simultaneously with independent tunable coefficients (most lack pure \(T\); those with pure \(T\) either lack \(T\epsilon^{p}\) or tie coefficients in a way GT does not satisfy).
